</div><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Vehicle propelled fully or mostly by electricity</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1320445320">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about all types of electric vehicles. For electric automobiles, see <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">Electric car</a>. For other uses of the term "EV", see <a href="/wiki/EV_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="EV (disambiguation)">EV</a>.</div>

decoding="async" width="200" height="133" class="mw-file-element" data-file-height="1643" /></a></span></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Semi_6_(cropped).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Tesla_Semi_6_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Tesla_Semi_6_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" class="mw-file-element" data-file-width="1174" data-file-height="783" /></a></span></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">Electric vehicles around the world <i>(left to right, from top)</i>:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">Electric car</a>: a <a href="/wiki/BMW_i3_(hatchback)" title="BMW i3 (hatchback)">BMW i3</a> charging from a standard electrical outlet.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Electric_aircraft" title="Electric aircraft">Electric aircraft</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Solar_Impulse_2" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar Impulse 2">Solar Impulse 2</a>, which <a href="/wiki/Circumnavigated" class="mw-redirect" title="Circumnavigated">circumnavigated</a> the globe</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Electric_boat" title="Electric boat">Electric boat</a>, the <i><a href="/wiki/China_Zorrilla_(ship)" title="China Zorrilla (ship)">China Zorrilla</a></i>, the largest battery electric vehicle ever built.</li>
<li>Electric <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail" title="High-speed rail">high speed train</a>: <a href="/wiki/N700_Series_Shinkansen" title="N700 Series Shinkansen">N700 Series Shinkansen</a> of <a href="/wiki/JR_Central" class="mw-redirect" title="JR Central">JR Central</a> on the <a href="/wiki/San%27yo_Shinkansen" class="mw-redirect" title="San&#39;yo Shinkansen">San'yo Shinkansen</a>, Japan</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_bus" title="Battery electric bus">Battery electric bus</a>: a <a href="/wiki/BYD_Company" title="BYD Company">BYD</a> bus in <a href="/wiki/Landskrona" title="Landskrona">Landskrona</a>, Sweden</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/E-bike" class="mw-redirect" title="E-bike">E-bike</a>, a Geero: with the removable battery integrated into the down tube.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Electric_truck" title="Electric truck">Electric truck</a>: <a href="/wiki/Class_8_truck" class="mw-redirect" title="Class 8 truck">Class 8</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Semi" title="Tesla Semi">Tesla Semi</a> in Rocklin,<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>California</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Neighborhood_Electric_Vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Neighborhood Electric Vehicle">Electric cart</a>: an <a href="/wiki/Italcar" title="Italcar">Italcar</a> Attiva C2S.4</li></ul></div></div></div></div>
<p>An <b>electric vehicle</b> (<b>EV</b>) is a vehicle propelled mostly by <a href="/wiki/Electric_power" title="Electric power">electric power</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> EVs encompass  <a href="/wiki/Road_vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Road vehicle">road</a> (<a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">cars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_bus" title="Electric bus">buses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_truck" title="Electric truck">trucks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Personal_transporter" title="Personal transporter">personal transporters</a>), <a href="/wiki/Rail_vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Rail vehicle">rail</a> (<a href="/wiki/Electric_locomotive" title="Electric locomotive">trains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trams" class="mw-redirect" title="Trams">trams</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monorails" class="mw-redirect" title="Monorails">monorails</a>), <a href="/wiki/Electric_boat" title="Electric boat">boats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Submersibles" class="mw-redirect" title="Submersibles">submersibles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_aircraft" title="Electric aircraft">aircraft</a> (<a href="/wiki/Fixed-wing" class="mw-redirect" title="Fixed-wing">fixed-wing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Multirotor" title="Multirotor">multirotors</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Electrically_powered_spacecraft_propulsion" class="mw-redirect" title="Electrically powered spacecraft propulsion">spacecraft</a>.
</p><p>EVs originated in the late 19th century. Electricity was among the preferred methods for powering early motor vehicles because it was quieter, provided comfort, and ease of operation. However, its limited range hindered mass adoption throughout the 20th century. <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">Internal combustion engines</a> were the dominant propulsion mechanisms for <a href="/wiki/Cars" class="mw-redirect" title="Cars">cars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trucks" class="mw-redirect" title="Trucks">trucks</a> for about 100 years, although electricity-powered locomotion became commonplace in other vehicle types, such as <a href="/wiki/Overhead_line" title="Overhead line">overhead line</a>-powered <a href="/wiki/Mass_transit" class="mw-redirect" title="Mass transit">mass transit</a> vehicles, as well as special purpose vehicles such as <a href="/wiki/Mobility_scooter" title="Mobility scooter">mobility scooters</a>.
</p><p>Since the late 20th century, technological advances in <a href="/wiki/Lithium_batteries" class="mw-redirect" title="Lithium batteries">lithium batteries</a>—which offer superior <a href="/wiki/Energy_density" title="Energy density">energy density</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electric_current" title="Electric current">current</a> output versus <a href="/wiki/Lead-acid_batteries" class="mw-redirect" title="Lead-acid batteries">lead-acid batteries</a>—has revived public interest as <a href="/wiki/Zero-emission_vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Zero-emission vehicle">zero-emission vehicle</a> options. Manufacturers mostly switched to <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Hybrid electric vehicle">hybrids</a> that use internal combustion engines like conventional vehicles, but add electric motors as a supplement, powered by electricity produced internally by <a href="/wiki/Motor-generators" class="mw-redirect" title="Motor-generators">motor-generators</a> and <a href="/wiki/Energy_recovery" title="Energy recovery">recovered</a> from <a href="/wiki/Regenerative_braking" title="Regenerative braking">regenerative braking</a>. <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid_electric_vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Plug-in hybrid electric vehicle">Plug-in hybrid electric vehicles</a>, which can be recharged from an <a href="/wiki/Electric_grid" class="mw-redirect" title="Electric grid">electric grid</a> and use electric motors as the primary propulsion rather than as a supplement to combustion engines, did not see any mass production until the late 2000s, and <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_car" class="mw-redirect" title="Battery electric car">battery electric cars</a> did not become practical options for the <a href="/wiki/Consumer_market" class="mw-redirect" title="Consumer market">consumer market</a> until the 2010s. Although <a href="/wiki/List_of_spacecraft_with_electric_propulsion" title="List of spacecraft with electric propulsion">spacecraft have been propelled by electricity</a> since the 1960s, <a href="/wiki/Non-rocket_spacelaunch" title="Non-rocket spacelaunch">non-rocket spacelaunch</a> from Earth remains science fiction.
</p>

href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1333133064" /><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1239400231">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar abbr{color:var(--color-base)!important}@media(prefers-color-scheme:dark){html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .navbar li a abbr{color:var(--color-base)!important}}@media print{.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:none!important}}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Sustainable_transport_sidebar" title="Template:Sustainable transport sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Sustainable_transport_sidebar" title="Template <p>Technological progresses in <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_batteries" class="mw-redirect" title="Electric vehicle batteries">electric vehicle batteries</a>, electric <a href="/wiki/Traction_motor" title="Traction motor">traction motors</a> and <a href="/wiki/Automotive_electronics" title="Automotive electronics">automotive electronics</a> (particularly <a href="/wiki/Electronic_control_unit" title="Electronic control unit">electronic control units</a>) has made electric cars more feasible and, in some cases, more cost-efficient than conventional ICE vehicles during the 21st century, with <a href="/wiki/Market_penetration" title="Market penetration">market penetration</a> in some countries like China reaching nearly half of all new vehicles sold.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As a means of reducing <a href="/wiki/Tailpipe_emission" class="mw-redirect" title="Tailpipe emission">tailpipe emissions</a> of <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gases" class="mw-redirect" title="Greenhouse gases">greenhouse gases</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Air_pollutant" class="mw-redirect" title="Air pollutant">air pollutants</a>, and to reduce the dependency on <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Government_incentive" class="mw-redirect" title="Government incentive">government incentives</a> are also available in many areas to promote the adoption of electric vehicles.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of 2026<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_industry_in_China" title="Electric vehicle industry in China">electric vehicle industry in China</a> produces more than the rest of the world combined.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_electric_vehicle" title="History of the electric vehicle">History of the electric vehicle</a></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Experimentation">Experimentation</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Experimentation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:EV1A014_(1)_cropped.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/EV1A014_%281%29_cropped.jpg/250px-EV1A014_%281%29_cropped.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/EV1A014_%281%29_cropped.jpg/500px-EV1A014_%281%29_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1173" data-file-height="782" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/General_Motors_EV1" title="General Motors EV1">General Motors EV1</a> electric car (1996–1998), a subject of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Who_Killed_the_Electric_Car%3F" title="Who Killed the Electric Car?">Who Killed the Electric Car?</a></i></figcaption></figure>
<p>In January 1990 <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> President introduced its EV concept two-seater, the "Impact", at the Los Angeles Auto Show. That September, the <a href="/wiki/California_Air_Resources_Board" title="California Air Resources Board">California Air Resources Board</a> mandated major-automaker sales of EVs, in phases starting in 1998. From 1996 to 1998 GM produced 1117 <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_EV1" title="General Motors EV1">EV1s</a>, 800 of which were made available through three-year leases.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Chrysler" title="Chrysler">Chrysler</a>, Ford, GM, <a href="/wiki/Honda" title="Honda">Honda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a> also produced limited numbers of EVs for California drivers during this period. In 2003, upon the expiration of GM's EV1 leases, GM discontinued them. The discontinuation has variously been attributed to: the auto industry's successful <a href="/wiki/United_States_federal_courts" class="mw-redirect" title="United States federal courts">federal court</a> challenge to California's <a href="/wiki/Zero-emissions_vehicle" title="Zero-emissions vehicle">zero-emissions vehicle</a> mandate, a federal regulation requiring GM to produce and maintain spare parts for the few thousand EV1s and the success of the oil and auto industries' media campaign to reduce public acceptance of EVs.
</p><p>A movie made on the subject in 2005–2006 was titled <i><a href="/wiki/Who_Killed_the_Electric_Car%3F" title="Who Killed the Electric Car?">Who Killed the Electric Car?</a></i> and released theatrically by <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Classics" title="Sony Pictures Classics">Sony Pictures Classics</a> in 2006. The film explores the roles of <a href="/wiki/Automobile_manufacturer" class="mw-redirect" title="Automobile manufacturer">automobile manufacturers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oil_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil industry">oil industry</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">U.S. government</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_battery" title="Electric battery">batteries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_(car)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydrogen (car)">hydrogen vehicles</a>, and the general public, and each of their roles in limiting the deployment and adoption of this technology.
</p><p>Ford released a number of their <a href="/wiki/Ford_Ecostar" title="Ford Ecostar">Ford Ecostar</a> delivery vans into the market. Honda, <a href="/wiki/Nissan" title="Nissan">Nissan</a> and Toyota also repossessed and crushed most of their EVs, which, like the GM EV1s, had been available only by closed-end lease. After public protests, Toyota sold 200 of its <a href="/wiki/Toyota_RAV4_EV" title="Toyota RAV4 EV">RAV4 EVs</a>; they later sold at over their original forty-thousand-dollar price. Later, <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a> of Canada sold off a number of Mini EVs when their Canadian testing ended.
</p><p>The production of the <a href="/wiki/Citro%C3%ABn_Berlingo_Electrique" class="mw-redirect" title="Citroën Berlingo Electrique">Citroën Berlingo Electrique</a> stopped in September 2005. <a href="/wiki/Zenn" class="mw-redirect" title="Zenn">Zenn</a> started production in 2006 but ended by 2009.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Reintroduction">Reintroduction</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Reintroduction"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1273380762/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" /><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:442px;max-width:442px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:206px;max-width:206px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:153px;overflow:hidden"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:2020%2B_Electric_vehicle_stock_-_International_Energy_Agency.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/2020%2B_Electric_vehicle_stock_-_International_Energy_Agency.svg/250px-2020%2B_Electric_vehicle_stock_-_International_Energy_Agency.svg.png" decoding="async" width="204" height="153" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/2020%2B_Electric_vehicle_stock_-_International_Energy_Agency.svg/500px-2020%2B_Electric_vehicle_stock_-_International_Energy_Agency.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="750" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">The global stock of both plug-in hybrid electric vehicles (PHEVs) and battery electric vehicles (BEVs) has grown steadily since the 2010s.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-IEA&#95;GlobalEVoutlook&#95;2023&#95;7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IEA_GlobalEVoutlook_2023-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:232px;max-width:232px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:153px;overflow:hidden"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Ev_sales_2012_2024_stacked.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Ev_sales_2012_2024_stacked.png/250px-Ev_sales_2012_2024_stacked.png" decoding="async" width="230" height="153" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Ev_sales_2012_2024_stacked.png/500px-Ev_sales_2012_2024_stacked.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">Sales of passenger electric vehicles (EVs) worldwide since 2012<sup id="cite&#95;ref-IEA2012–24&#95;8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IEA2012–24-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>During the late 20th and early 21st century, the <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_with_petroleum" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental issues with petroleum">environmental impact</a> of the petroleum-based transportation infrastructure, along with the fear of <a href="/wiki/Peak_oil" title="Peak oil">peak oil</a>, led to renewed interest in electric transportation infrastructure.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Eberle&#95;Von&#95;Helmolt20102&#95;9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eberle_Von_Helmolt20102-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By the 21st century an <a href="/wiki/Energy_transition" title="Energy transition">energy transition</a> to <a href="/wiki/Electrify" class="mw-redirect" title="Electrify">electrify</a> as many things as possible, not just vehicles, rather than burning stuff became to be seen as very important for human health and the environment.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> EVs differ from <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuel</a>-powered vehicles in that the electricity they consume can be generated from a wide range of sources, including <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels" class="mw-redirect" title="Fossil fuels">fossil fuels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear power</a>, and renewables such as <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind power</a>, or any combination of those. Recent advancements in battery technology and charging infrastructure have addressed many of the earlier barriers to EV adoption, making electric vehicles a more viable option for a wider range of consumers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Carbon_footprint" title="Carbon footprint">carbon footprint</a> and other emissions of electric vehicles vary depending on the fuel and technology used for <a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">electricity generation</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-NotterKouravelou20152&#95;13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NotterKouravelou20152-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The electricity may be stored in the vehicle using a battery, flywheel, or <a href="/wiki/Supercapacitor" title="Supercapacitor">Supercapacitor</a>S. Vehicles using <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engines" class="mw-redirect" title="Internal combustion engines">internal combustion engines</a> usually only derive their energy from a single or a few sources, usually non-renewable fossil fuels. A key advantage of electric vehicles is <a href="/wiki/Regenerative_braking" title="Regenerative braking">regenerative braking</a>, which recovers <a href="/wiki/Kinetic_energy" title="Kinetic energy">kinetic energy</a>, typically lost during <a href="/wiki/Friction_braking" class="mw-redirect" title="Friction braking">friction braking</a> as heat, as electricity restored to the on-board battery. Although over 20% of new cars sold in 2024 were electric only 2% of trucks were.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> China is the world's leading EV producer, accounting for more than 70% of global production and 67% of global sales of electric vehicles in 2024.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Electricity_sources">Electricity sources</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Electricity sources"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1273380762/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" /><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:2402_%27County_of_Hampshire%27_at_Wool.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/2402_%27County_of_Hampshire%27_at_Wool.JPG/500px-2402_%27County_of_Hampshire%27_at_Wool.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">A passenger train, taking power through a <a href="/wiki/Third_rail" title="Third rail">third rail</a> with return through the traction rails</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:SwissMGB.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/SwissMGB.jpg/250px-SwissMGB.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="149" <th>Fuel used
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">Combustion-only vehicle</a><br />(ICE)</td>
<td>Exclusively uses <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a> or other fuel.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Start-stop_system" title="Start-stop system">Micro hybrid electric vehicle</a><br />(μHEV)</td>
<td>Exclusively uses petroleum or other fuel,<br />but can shut off engine to consume less.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Mild_hybrid" title="Mild hybrid">Mild hybrid electric vehicle</a><br />(MHEV, BAHV)</td>
<td>Exclusively uses petroleum or other fuel,<br />but has electric battery to consume less.
</td></tr>

<td>Uses mixture of petroleum or other fuel<br />and electricity from <a href="/wiki/Electrical_grid" title="Electrical grid">power grid</a>.
</td></tr>

<td>Exclusively uses electricity from power grid.
</td></tr>
