<td>Exclusively uses <a href="/wiki/Compressed_hydrogen" title="Compressed hydrogen">hydrogen</a> or other fuel<br />to generate electricity.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:right"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1333133064" /><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1239400231" /><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Electric_vehicle" title="Template:Electric vehicle"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Electric_vehicle" title="Template talk:Electric vehicle"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Template:Electric_vehicle" title="Special:EditPage/Template:Electric vehicle"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>EVs are much more efficient than <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engines" class="mw-redirect" title="Internal combustion engines">internal combustion engines</a> and have few direct emissions. At the same time, they do rely on electrical energy that is generally provided by a combination of non-fossil fuel plants and fossil fuel plants.
</p><p>There are many ways to generate electricity, of varying costs, efficiency and ecological desirability. EVs can be made less polluting overall by modifying the source of electricity. In some areas, individuals can ask utilities to provide their electricity from renewable energy. Therefore, it gives the greatest degree of <a href="/wiki/Energy_resilience" class="mw-redirect" title="Energy resilience">energy resilience</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Connection_to_generator_plants">Connection to generator plants</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Connection to generator plants"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>Direct connection to <a href="/wiki/Electric_grid" class="mw-redirect" title="Electric grid">electric grids</a> as is common among <a href="/wiki/Electric_trains" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Electric trains">electric trains</a>, trams, <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">trolleybuses</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Trolleytruck" title="Trolleytruck">trolleytrucks</a> (see also: <a href="/wiki/Overhead_lines" class="mw-redirect" title="Overhead lines">overhead lines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Third_rail" title="Third rail">third rail</a> and <a href="/wiki/Conduit_current_collection" title="Conduit current collection">conduit current collection</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Online_electric_vehicle" title="Online electric vehicle">Online electric vehicle</a> collects power from electric power strips buried under the road surface through <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_induction" title="Electromagnetic induction">electromagnetic induction</a></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Onboard_generators_and_hybrid_EVs">Onboard generators and hybrid EVs</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Onboard generators and hybrid EVs"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Diesel%E2%80%93electric_transmission" class="mw-redirect" title="Diesel–electric transmission">Diesel–electric transmission</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petrol%E2%80%93electric_transmission" title="Petrol–electric transmission">Petrol–electric transmission</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle" title="Hybrid vehicle">Hybrid vehicle</a></div>
<ul><li>Generated on-board using a diesel engine: <a href="/wiki/Diesel%E2%80%93electric_transmission" class="mw-redirect" title="Diesel–electric transmission">diesel–electric</a> locomotive and diesel–electric multiple unit (DEMU)</li>
<li>Generated on-board using a <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell" title="Fuel cell">fuel cell</a>: <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell_vehicle" title="Fuel cell vehicle">fuel cell vehicle</a></li>
<li>Generated on-board using <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear power</a>: nuclear <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carriers</a></li>
<li>Renewable sources such as <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a>: <a href="/wiki/Solar_vehicle" title="Solar vehicle">solar vehicle</a></li></ul>
<p>It is also possible to have hybrid EVs that derive electricity from multiple sources, such as:
</p>
<ul><li>On-board rechargeable electricity storage system (RESS) and a direct continuous connection to land-based generation plants for purposes of on-highway recharging with unrestricted highway range<sup id="cite&#95;ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>On-board rechargeable electricity storage system and a fueled propulsion power source (internal combustion engine): plug-in hybrid</li></ul>
<p>For especially large EVs, such as <a href="/wiki/Submarines" class="mw-redirect" title="Submarines">submarines</a>, the chemical energy of the diesel–electric can be replaced by a <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reactor" title="Nuclear reactor">nuclear reactor</a>. The nuclear reactor usually provides heat, which drives a <a href="/wiki/Steam_turbine" title="Steam turbine">steam turbine</a>, which drives a generator, which is then fed to the propulsion. <i>See <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_marine_propulsion" title="Nuclear marine propulsion">Nuclear marine propulsion</a>.</i>
</p><p>A few experimental vehicles, such as some cars and a handful of aircraft use <a href="/wiki/Solar_panel" title="Solar panel">solar panels</a> for electricity.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Onboard_storage">Onboard storage</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Onboard storage"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>These systems are powered from an external generator plant (nearly always when stationary), and then disconnected before motion occurs, and the electricity is stored in the vehicle until needed.
</p>
<ul><li>Full Electric Vehicles (FEV).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Power storage methods include:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Chemical_energy" title="Chemical energy">Chemical energy</a> stored on the vehicle in on-board batteries: <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_vehicle" title="Battery electric vehicle">Battery electric vehicle</a> (BEV) typically with a <a href="/wiki/Lithium-ion_battery" title="Lithium-ion battery">lithium-ion battery</a></li>
<li>Kinetic energy storage: <a href="/wiki/Gyrobus" title="Gyrobus">flywheels</a></li>
<li>Static energy stored on the vehicle in on-board <a href="/wiki/Electric_double-layer_capacitor" class="mw-redirect" title="Electric double-layer capacitor">electric double-layer capacitors</a></li></ul></li></ul>
<p>Batteries, <a href="/wiki/Electric_double-layer_capacitor" class="mw-redirect" title="Electric double-layer capacitor">electric double-layer capacitors</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flywheel_energy_storage" title="Flywheel energy storage">flywheel energy storage</a> are forms of rechargeable on-board electricity storage systems. By avoiding an intermediate mechanical step, the <a href="/wiki/Energy_conversion_efficiency" title="Energy conversion efficiency">energy conversion efficiency</a> can be improved compared to hybrids by avoiding unnecessary energy conversions. Furthermore, electro-chemical batteries conversions are reversible, allowing electrical energy to be stored in chemical form.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Components">Components</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Components"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The type of <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_battery" title="Electric vehicle battery">battery</a>, the type of <a href="/wiki/Traction_motor" title="Traction motor">traction motor</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Motor_controller" title="Motor controller">motor controller</a> design vary according to the size, power and proposed application, which can be as small as a <a href="/wiki/Motorized_shopping_cart" title="Motorized shopping cart">motorized shopping cart</a> or <a href="/wiki/Wheelchair" title="Wheelchair">wheelchair</a>, through <a href="/wiki/Pedelec" title="Pedelec">pedelecs</a>, electric motorcycles and scooters, neighborhood electric vehicles, industrial <a href="/wiki/Fork-lift_truck" class="mw-redirect" title="Fork-lift truck">fork-lift trucks</a> and including many hybrid vehicles.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Battery">Battery</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Battery"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_battery" title="Electric vehicle battery">Electric vehicle battery</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Nissan_Leaf_battery_pack_DC_03_2011_1629.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Nissan_Leaf_battery_pack_DC_03_2011_1629.jpg/250px-Nissan_Leaf_battery_pack_DC_03_2011_1629.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Nissan_Leaf_battery_pack_DC_03_2011_1629.jpg/500px-Nissan_Leaf_battery_pack_DC_03_2011_1629.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" /></a><figcaption>A <a href="/wiki/Lithium-ion_battery" title="Lithium-ion battery">lithium-ion battery</a> pack of the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Leaf" title="Nissan Leaf">Nissan Leaf</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>An electric-vehicle battery (EVB) in addition to the traction battery specialty systems used for industrial (or recreational) vehicles, are batteries used to power the propulsion system of a battery electric vehicle (BEVs). These batteries are usually a secondary (rechargeable) battery, and are typically lithium-ion batteries.
</p><p>Traction batteries, specifically designed with a high ampere-hour capacity, are used in forklifts, electric golf carts, riding floor scrubbers, electric motorcycles, electric cars, trucks, vans, and other electric vehicles.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Seitz19942&#95;22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seitz19942-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Tofield19852&#95;23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tofield19852-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Lithium-ion_battery">Lithium-ion battery</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Lithium-ion battery"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:2010-_Battery_prices_for_electric_vehicles.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/2010-_Battery_prices_for_electric_vehicles.svg/250px-2010-_Battery_prices_for_electric_vehicles.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="141" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/2010-_Battery_prices_for_electric_vehicles.svg/500px-2010-_Battery_prices_for_electric_vehicles.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="675" /></a><figcaption>Battery prices fell, given economies of scale and new cell chemistries improving energy density.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-BloombergNEF&#95;202207212&#95;24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BloombergNEF_202207212-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, general inflationary pressures, and rising costs of raw materials and components, inhibited price declines in the early 2020s.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-BloombergNEF&#95;202207212&#95;24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BloombergNEF_202207212-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>Since their first commercial release in 1991, <a href="/wiki/Lithium-ion_batteries" class="mw-redirect" title="Lithium-ion batteries">lithium-ion batteries</a> have become an important technology for achieving low-carbon transportation systems. Most electric vehicles use lithium-ion batteries (Li-Ions or LIBs). Lithium-ion batteries have a higher <a href="/wiki/Energy_density" title="Energy density">energy density</a>, longer <a href="/wiki/Rechargeable_battery#Lifespan_and_cycle_stability" title="Rechargeable battery">life span</a>, and higher <a href="/wiki/Power_density" title="Power density">power density</a> than most other practical batteries.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Complicating factors include safety, durability, thermal breakdown, <a href="/wiki/Lithium-ion_battery#Environmental_impact" title="Lithium-ion battery">environmental impact</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rechargeable_battery#Price_history" title="Rechargeable battery">cost</a>. Li-ion batteries should be used within safe temperature and voltage ranges to operate safely and efficiently.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-LuHan20132&#95;26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LuHan20132-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Increasing the battery's lifespan decreases effective costs and environmental impact. One technique is to operate a subset of the battery cells at a time and switching these subsets.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-AdanyAurbach20132&#95;27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AdanyAurbach20132-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the past, <a href="/wiki/Nickel%E2%80%93metal_hydride_batteries" class="mw-redirect" title="Nickel–metal hydride batteries">nickel–metal hydride batteries</a> were used in some electric cars, such as those made by General Motors.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These battery types are considered outdated due to their tendencies to self-discharge in the heat.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Furthermore, a patent for this type of battery was held by Chevron, which created a problem for their widespread development.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These factors, coupled with their high cost, has led to lithium-ion batteries leading as the predominant battery for EVs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The prices of lithium-ion batteries have declined dramatically over the past decade, contributing to a reduction in price for electric vehicles, but an increase in the price of critical minerals such as lithium from 2021 to the end of 2022 has put pressure on historical battery price decreases.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Electric_motor">Electric motor</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Electric motor"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Iveco_Stralis_AD_190_E-truck._Lidl._Spielvogel.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Iveco_Stralis_AD_190_E-truck._Lidl._Spielvogel.jpg/250px-Iveco_Stralis_AD_190_E-truck._Lidl._Spielvogel.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Iveco_Stralis_AD_190_E-truck._Lidl._Spielvogel.jpg/500px-Iveco_Stralis_AD_190_E-truck._Lidl._Spielvogel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4923" data-file-height="3282" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Electric_truck" title="Electric truck">Electric truck</a> e-Force One</figcaption></figure>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Traction_motor" title="Traction motor">Traction motor</a></div>
<p>The power of a vehicle's <a href="/wiki/Electric_motor" title="Electric motor">electric motor</a>, as in other machines, is measured in kilowatts (kW). Electric motors can deliver their maximum torque over a wide RPM range. This means that the performance of a vehicle with a 100&#160;kW electric motor exceeds that of a vehicle with a 100&#160;kW internal combustion engine, which can only deliver its maximum torque within a limited range of engine speed.
</p><p>Efficiency of charging varies considerably depending on the type of charger,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and energy is lost during the process of converting the electrical energy to mechanical energy.
</p><p>Usually, <a href="/wiki/Direct_current" title="Direct current">direct current</a> (DC) electricity is fed into a DC/AC inverter where it is converted to <a href="/wiki/Alternating_current" title="Alternating current">alternating current</a> (AC) electricity and this AC electricity is connected to a 3-phase AC motor.
</p><p>For electric trains, forklift trucks, and some electric cars, DC motors are often used. In some cases, <a href="/wiki/Universal_motor" title="Universal motor">universal motors</a> are used, and then AC or DC may be employed. In recent production vehicles, various motor types have been implemented; for instance, <a href="/wiki/Induction_motor" title="Induction motor">induction motors</a> within <a href="/wiki/Tesla,_Inc." title="Tesla, Inc.">Tesla</a> vehicles and permanent magnet machines in the <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Leaf" title="Nissan Leaf">Nissan Leaf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Bolt" title="Chevrolet Bolt">Chevrolet Bolt</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-WidmerMartin20152&#95;35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WidmerMartin20152-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Energy_and_motors">Energy and motors</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Energy and motors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Electric_powertrain.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Electric_powertrain.jpg/250px-Electric_powertrain.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="96" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c2/Electric_powertrain.jpg 2x" data-file-width="390" data-file-height="150" /></a><figcaption>An electric <a href="/wiki/Powertrain" title="Powertrain">powertrain</a> used by <a href="/wiki/Power_Vehicle_Innovation" title="Power Vehicle Innovation">Power Vehicle Innovation</a> for trucks or buses<sup id="cite&#95;ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1273380762/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" /><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:244px;max-width:244px"><div class="trow"><div class="theader"><a href="/wiki/Tesla_Model_S" title="Tesla Model S">Tesla Model S</a> drive motor</div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:242px;max-width:242px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Motors_Model_S_base.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Tesla_Motors_Model_S_base.JPG/250px-Tesla_Motors_Model_S_base.JPG" decoding="async" width="240" height="160" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Tesla_Motors_Model_S_base.JPG/500px-Tesla_Motors_Model_S_base.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2153" data-file-height="1431" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">Mounted on chassis</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:242px;max-width:242px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Model_S_motor_cutout.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Tesla_Model_S_motor_cutout.jpg/250px-Tesla_Model_S_motor_cutout.jpg" decoding="async" width="240" height="180" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Tesla_Model_S_motor_cutout.jpg/500px-Tesla_Model_S_motor_cutout.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">Cutaway view</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Electric motors are mechanically very simple and often achieve 90% <a href="/wiki/Energy_conversion_efficiency" title="Energy conversion efficiency">energy conversion efficiency</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> over the full range of speeds and power output and can be precisely controlled.
</p><p>Motion is provided by a <a href="/wiki/Rotary_motor" class="mw-redirect" title="Rotary motor">rotary</a> electric motor. However, it is possible to "unroll" the motor to drive directly against a special matched track. These <a href="/wiki/Linear_motor" title="Linear motor">linear motors</a> are used in <a href="/wiki/Maglev_train" class="mw-redirect" title="Maglev train">maglev trains</a> which float above the rails supported by <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_levitation" title="Magnetic levitation">magnetic levitation</a>. This allows for almost no rolling resistance of the vehicle and no mechanical wear and tear of the train or track. In addition to the high-performance control systems needed, <a href="/wiki/Railroad_switch" title="Railroad switch">switching</a> and curving of the tracks becomes difficult with linear motors, which to date has restricted their operations to high-speed point to point services.
</p><p>Electric traction allows the use of <a href="/wiki/Regenerative_braking" title="Regenerative braking">regenerative braking</a>, in which the motors are used as brakes and become generators that transform the motion of, usually, a train into electrical power that is then fed back into the lines. This system is particularly advantageous in mountainous operations, as descending vehicles can produce a large portion of the power required for those ascending, and in start-and-stop city use. This regenerative system is only viable if the system is large enough to use the power generated by descending vehicles.
</p><p>They can be finely controlled and provide high <a href="/wiki/Torque" title="Torque">torque</a> from stationary-to-moving, unlike internal combustion engines, and do not need multiple gears to match power curves. This removes the need for <a href="/wiki/Transmission_(mechanics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Transmission (mechanics)">gearboxes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Torque_converter" title="Torque converter">torque converters</a>.
</p><p>EVs provide quiet and smooth operation and consequently have less noise and <a href="/wiki/Vibration" title="Vibration">vibration</a> than internal combustion engines.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ec.europa.eu2&#95;38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ec.europa.eu2-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> While this is a desirable attribute, it has also evoked concern that the absence of the usual sounds of an approaching vehicle poses a danger to blind, elderly and very young pedestrians. To mitigate this situation, many countries mandate <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_warning_sounds" title="Electric vehicle warning sounds">warning sounds</a> when EVs are moving slowly, up to a speed when normal motion and rotation (road, suspension, electric motor, etc.) noises become audible.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Electric motors do not require oxygen, unlike internal combustion engines; this is useful for <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarines</a> and for <a href="/wiki/Rover_(space_exploration)" title="Rover (space exploration)">space rovers</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Types">Types</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Types"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Squad_Solar_Car_(Fully_Charged_2022).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Squad_Solar_Car_%28Fully_Charged_2022%29.jpg/250px-Squad_Solar_Car_%28Fully_Charged_2022%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="210" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Squad_Solar_Car_%28Fully_Charged_2022%29.jpg/500px-Squad_Solar_Car_%28Fully_Charged_2022%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2784" data-file-height="2344" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Neighborhood_Electric_Vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Neighborhood Electric Vehicle">Neighborhood Electric Vehicle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Squad_Solar" title="Squad Solar">Squad Solar</a> NEV, with solar panel roof</figcaption></figure>
<p>It is generally possible to equip any kind of vehicle with an electric power-train.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Ground_vehicles">Ground vehicles</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Ground vehicles"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Pure-electric_vehicles">Pure-electric vehicles</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Pure-electric vehicles"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">Electric car</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_vehicle" title="Battery electric vehicle">Battery electric vehicle</a></div>
<p>A pure-electric vehicle or all-electric vehicle is powered exclusively through electric motors. The electricity may come from a battery (<a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_vehicle" title="Battery electric vehicle">battery electric vehicle</a>), solar panel (<a href="/wiki/Solar_vehicle" title="Solar vehicle">solar vehicle</a>) or fuel cell (<a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell_vehicle" title="Fuel cell vehicle">fuel cell vehicle</a>).
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Hybrids">Hybrids</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Hybrids"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="excerpt-block"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066933788">.mw-parser-output .excerpt-hat .mw-editsection-like{font-style:normal}</style><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Hybrid electric vehicle">Hybrid electric vehicle</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hybrid_electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Hybrid electric vehicle">hybrid electric vehicle</a> (HEV) is a type of <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle" title="Hybrid vehicle">hybrid vehicle</a> that couples a conventional <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">internal combustion engine</a> (ICE) with one or more <a href="/wiki/Electric_engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Electric engine">electric engines</a> into a <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle_drivetrain" title="Hybrid vehicle drivetrain">combined propulsion system</a>. The presence of the electric <a href="/wiki/Powertrain" title="Powertrain">powertrain</a>, which has inherently better <a href="/wiki/Energy_conversion_efficiency" title="Energy conversion efficiency">energy conversion efficiency</a>, is intended to achieve either better <a href="/wiki/Fuel_economy_in_automobiles" title="Fuel economy in automobiles">fuel economy</a> or better <a href="/wiki/Acceleration" title="Acceleration">acceleration</a> performance than a <a href="/wiki/Conventional_vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Conventional vehicle">conventional vehicle</a>. There is a variety of HEV types and the degree to which each functions as an electric vehicle (EV) also varies. The most common form of HEV is hybrid electric <a href="/wiki/Passenger_car" class="mw-redirect" title="Passenger car">passenger cars</a>, although hybrid electric <a href="/wiki/Truck" title="Truck">trucks</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pickup_truck" title="Pickup truck">pickups</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tow_truck" title="Tow truck">tow trucks</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tractor" title="Tractor">tractors</a>), <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">buses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motorboat" title="Motorboat">motorboats</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Hybrid&#95;electric&#95;vehicle&#95;HybridCarHist&#95;41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hybrid_electric_vehicle_HybridCarHist-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Aircraft" title="Aircraft">aircraft</a> also exist.
</p><p>Modern HEVs use <a href="/wiki/Energy_recovery" title="Energy recovery">energy recovery</a> technologies such as <a href="/wiki/Motor%E2%80%93generator" title="Motor–generator">motor–generator</a> units and <a href="/wiki/Regenerative_braking" title="Regenerative braking">regenerative braking</a> to recycle the vehicle's <a href="/wiki/Kinetic_energy" title="Kinetic energy">kinetic energy</a> to <a href="/wiki/Electric_energy" class="mw-redirect" title="Electric energy">electric energy</a> via an <a href="/wiki/Alternator_(automotive)" title="Alternator (automotive)">alternator</a>, which is <a href="/wiki/Energy_storage" title="Energy storage">stored</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_battery" title="Electric vehicle battery">battery pack</a> or a <a href="/wiki/Supercapacitor" title="Supercapacitor">supercapacitor</a>. Some varieties of HEV use an internal combustion engine to directly drive an <a href="/wiki/Electrical_generator" class="mw-redirect" title="Electrical generator">electrical generator</a>, which either recharges the vehicle's batteries or directly powers the electric <a href="/wiki/Traction_motor" title="Traction motor">traction motors</a>; this combination is known as a <a href="/wiki/Range_extender" title="Range extender">range extender</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Many HEVs <a href="/wiki/Idle_reduction" title="Idle reduction">reduce idle emissions</a> by temporarily shutting down the combustion engine at <a href="/wiki/Idle_(engine)" title="Idle (engine)">idle</a> (such as when waiting at the <a href="/wiki/Traffic_light" title="Traffic light">traffic light</a>) and restarting it when needed; this is known as a <a href="/wiki/Start-stop_system" title="Start-stop system">start-stop system</a>. A hybrid-electric system produces less <a href="/wiki/Tailpipe_emission" class="mw-redirect" title="Tailpipe emission">tailpipe emissions</a> than a comparably sized <a href="/wiki/Petrol_engine" title="Petrol engine">petrol engine</a> vehicle since the hybrid's petrol engine usually has smaller <a href="/wiki/Engine_displacement" title="Engine displacement">displacement</a> and thus lower <a href="/wiki/Fuel_consumption" class="mw-redirect" title="Fuel consumption">fuel consumption</a> than that of a conventional petrol-powered vehicle. If the engine is not used to drive the car directly, it can be geared to run at maximum efficiency, further improving fuel economy.
</p>
</div></div>
<p>There are different ways that a hybrid electric vehicle can combine the power from an electric motor and the internal combustion engine. The most common type is a <b>parallel hybrid</b> that connects the engine and the electric motor to the wheels through mechanical coupling. In this scenario, the electric motor and the engine can drive the wheels directly. <b>Series hybrids</b> only use the electric motor to drive the wheels and can often be referred to as extended-range electric vehicles (EREVs) or range-extended electric vehicles (REEVs). There are also <b>series–parallel hybrids</b> where the vehicle can be powered by the engine working alone, the electric motor on its own, or by both working together; this is designed so that the engine can run at its optimum range as often as possible.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Plug-ins">Plug-ins</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Plug-ins"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">Plug-in electric vehicle</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">Plug-in hybrid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">Electric car</a></div>
<p>A plug-in electric vehicle (PEV) is any <a href="/wiki/Motor_vehicle" title="Motor vehicle">motor vehicle</a> that can be recharged from any external source of electricity, such as <a href="/wiki/Wall_socket" class="mw-redirect" title="Wall socket">wall sockets</a>, and the electricity stored in the <a href="/wiki/Rechargeable_battery" title="Rechargeable battery">Rechargeable battery</a> packs drives or contributes to drive the wheels. PEV is a subcategory of electric vehicles that includes <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_vehicle" title="Battery electric vehicle">battery electric vehicles</a> (BEVs), plug-in hybrid vehicles, (PHEVs), and <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_conversion" title="Electric vehicle conversion">electric vehicle conversions</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Hybrid electric vehicle">hybrid electric vehicles</a> and conventional <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">internal combustion engine</a> vehicles.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-PEVs2&#95;44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PEVs2-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-CSE2&#95;45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSE2-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Range-extended">Range-extended</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Range-extended"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Range_extender" title="Range extender">Range extender</a></div>
<p>A range-extended electric vehicle (REEV) is a vehicle powered by an electric motor and a plug-in battery. An auxiliary combustion engine is used only to supplement battery charging and not as the primary source of power.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="On-_and_off-road">On- and off-road</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: On- and off-road"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>On-road electric vehicles include electric cars, electric trolleybuses, <a href="/wiki/Electric_bus" title="Electric bus">electric buses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_bus" title="Battery electric bus">battery electric buses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_truck" title="Electric truck">electric trucks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_bicycle" title="Electric bicycle">electric bicycles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_motorcycles_and_scooters" title="Electric motorcycles and scooters">electric motorcycles and scooters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Personal_transporter" title="Personal transporter">personal transporters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neighborhood_electric_vehicle" title="Neighborhood electric vehicle">neighborhood electric vehicles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golf_cart" title="Golf cart">golf carts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milk_float" title="Milk float">milk floats</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Forklift" title="Forklift">forklifts</a>. <a href="/wiki/Off-road_vehicle" title="Off-road vehicle">Off-road vehicles</a> include electrified <a href="/wiki/All-terrain_vehicle" title="All-terrain vehicle">all-terrain vehicles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electric_tractor" title="Electric tractor">electric tractors</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Trucks">Trucks</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Trucks"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:E-Truck_Renault_Midlum_Electric.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/E-Truck_Renault_Midlum_Electric.jpg/250px-E-Truck_Renault_Midlum_Electric.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="179" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/E-Truck_Renault_Midlum_Electric.jpg/500px-E-Truck_Renault_Midlum_Electric.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3616" data-file-height="2583" /></a><figcaption>Electric <a href="/wiki/Renault_Midlum" title="Renault Midlum">Renault Midlum</a> used by <a href="/wiki/Nestl%C3%A9" title="Nestlé">Nestlé</a> in 2015</figcaption></figure>
<p>An <b>electric truck</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_vehicle" title="Battery electric vehicle">battery electric vehicle</a> (BEV) designed to transport cargo, carry specialized payloads, or perform other utilitarian work.
</p><p>Electric trucks have serviced niche applications like <a href="/wiki/Milk_float" title="Milk float">milk floats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ground_support_equipment#Pushback_tugs_and_tractors" title="Ground support equipment">pushback tugs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Forklift#Battery-electric" title="Forklift">forklifts</a> for over a hundred years, typically using <a href="/wiki/Lead%E2%80%93acid_batteries" class="mw-redirect" title="Lead–acid batteries">lead–acid batteries</a>, but the rapid development of lighter and more energy-dense <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_battery#Electric_vehicle_battery_types" title="Electric vehicle battery">battery chemistries</a> in the twenty-first century has broadened the range of applicability of electric propulsion to trucks in many more roles.
</p><p>Electric trucks reduce noise and pollution, relative to internal-combustion trucks. Due to the high efficiency and low component-counts of electric power trains, no fuel burning while idle, and silent and efficient acceleration, the costs of owning and operating electric trucks are dramatically lower than their predecessors.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_the_American_trucking_industry#Over-the-road" title="Glossary of the American trucking industry">Long-distance freight</a> has been the trucking segment least amenable to electrification, since the increased weight of batteries, relative to fuel, detracts from payload capacity, and the alternative, more frequent recharging, detracts from delivery time. By contrast, short-haul urban delivery has been electrified rapidly, since the clean and quiet nature of electric trucks fit well with urban planning and municipal regulation, and the capacities of reasonably sized batteries are well-suited to daily stop-and-go traffic within a metropolitan area.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Railborne">Railborne</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Railborne"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Railway_electrification_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Railway electrification system">Railway electrification system</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:2001-03-31.H-TW2000-Vahrenwalder-Platz.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/2001-03-31.H-TW2000-Vahrenwalder-Platz.jpg/250px-2001-03-31.H-TW2000-Vahrenwalder-Platz.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="186" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/2001-03-31.H-TW2000-Vahrenwalder-Platz.jpg/500px-2001-03-31.H-TW2000-Vahrenwalder-Platz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1131" data-file-height="840" /></a><figcaption>A tram (or streetcar) in <a href="/wiki/Hanover" title="Hanover">Hanover</a> drawing current from a single overhead wire through a <a href="/wiki/Pantograph_(rail)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pantograph (rail)">pantograph</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>The fixed nature of a rail line makes it relatively easy to power EVs through permanent <a href="/wiki/Overhead_lines" class="mw-redirect" title="Overhead lines">overhead lines</a> or electrified <a href="/wiki/Third_rail" title="Third rail">third rails</a>, eliminating the need for heavy onboard batteries. <a href="/wiki/Electric_locomotive" title="Electric locomotive">Electric locomotives</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_multiple_unit" title="Electric multiple unit">electric multiple units</a>, electric trams (also called streetcars or trolleys), electric <a href="/wiki/Light_rail_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Light rail system">light rail systems</a>, and electric <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">rapid transit</a> are all in common use today, especially in Europe and Asia.
</p><p>Since electric trains do not need to carry a heavy internal combustion engine or large batteries, they can have very good <a href="/wiki/Power-to-weight_ratio" title="Power-to-weight ratio">power-to-weight ratios</a>. This allows <a href="/wiki/High_speed_train" class="mw-redirect" title="High speed train">high speed trains</a> such as France's double-deck <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">TGVs</a> to operate at speeds of 320&#160;km/h (200&#160;mph) or higher, and <a href="/wiki/Electric_locomotive" title="Electric locomotive">electric locomotives</a> to have a much higher power output than <a href="/wiki/Diesel_locomotive" title="Diesel locomotive">diesel locomotives</a>. In addition, they have higher short-term <a href="/wiki/Overcurrent" title="Overcurrent">surge power</a> for fast acceleration, and using <a href="/wiki/Regenerative_brake" class="mw-redirect" title="Regenerative brake">regenerative brakes</a> can put braking power back into the <a href="/wiki/Electrical_grid" title="Electrical grid">electrical grid</a> rather than wasting it.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Maglev_(transport)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maglev (transport)">Maglev</a> trains are also nearly always EVs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>There are also <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_multiple_unit" title="Battery electric multiple unit">battery electric passenger trains</a> operating on non-electrified rail lines.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading5"><h5 id="Hydrogen_trains">Hydrogen trains</h5><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Hydrogen trains"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Particularly in Europe, <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_train" title="Hydrogen train">fuel-cell electric trains</a> are gaining in popularity to replace <a href="/wiki/Diesel%E2%80%93electric_locomotive" class="mw-redirect" title="Diesel–electric locomotive">diesel–electric locomotive</a> units. In Germany, several <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">Länder</a> have ordered <a href="/wiki/Alstom_Coradia_LINT" title="Alstom Coradia LINT">Alstom Coradia iLINT</a> trainsets, in service since 2018,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-France-Presse2&#95;54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-France-Presse2-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> with France also planning to order trainsets.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The United Kingdom, the Netherlands, Denmark, Norway, Italy, Canada<sup id="cite&#95;ref-France-Presse2&#95;54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-France-Presse2-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and Mexico<sup id="cite&#95;ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are equally interested. In France, the <a href="/wiki/SNCF" title="SNCF">SNCF</a> plans to replace all its remaining diesel-electric trains with hydrogen trains by 2035.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the United Kingdom, Alstom announced in 2018 their plan to retrofit British Rail Class 321 trainsets with fuel cells.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Watercraft">Watercraft</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Watercraft"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Submarine#Propulsion" title="Submarine">Submarine §&#160;Propulsion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ship#Propulsion_systems" title="Ship">Ship §&#160;Propulsion systems</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Electric_boat" title="Electric boat">electric boat</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Oceanvolt_sd8.6_electric_saildrive_motor.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Oceanvolt_sd8.6_electric_saildrive_motor.jpg/250px-Oceanvolt_sd8.6_electric_saildrive_motor.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="358" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/08/Oceanvolt_sd8.6_electric_saildrive_motor.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="572" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Oceanvolt" title="Oceanvolt">Oceanvolt</a> SD8.6 electric saildrive motor</figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/Electric_boat" title="Electric boat">Electric boats</a> were popular around the turn of the 20th century. Interest in quiet and potentially renewable marine transportation has steadily increased since the late 20th century, as <a href="/wiki/Solar_cells" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar cells">solar cells</a> have given <a href="/wiki/Motorboat" title="Motorboat">motorboats</a> the infinite range of <a href="/wiki/Sailboats" class="mw-redirect" title="Sailboats">sailboats</a>. Electric motors can and have also been used in sailboats instead of traditional diesel engines.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Electric ferries operate routinely.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">Submarines</a> use batteries (charged by <a href="/wiki/Diesel-electric_transmission" class="mw-redirect" title="Diesel-electric transmission">diesel</a> or gasoline engines at the surface), <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_submarine" title="Nuclear submarine">nuclear</a> power, <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell" title="Fuel cell">fuel cells</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Stirling_engine" title="Stirling engine">Stirling engines</a> to run electric motor-driven propellers. Fully electric tugboats are being used in Auckland, New Zealand (June 2022),<sup id="cite&#95;ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Vancouver, British Columbia (October 2023),<sup id="cite&#95;ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and San Diego, California.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Aircraft">Aircraft</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Aircraft"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mars_helicopter_on_sol_46.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Mars_helicopter_on_sol_46.png/250px-Mars_helicopter_on_sol_46.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="250" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Mars_helicopter_on_sol_46.png/500px-Mars_helicopter_on_sol_46.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Ingenuity_(helicopter)" title="Ingenuity (helicopter)">Mars helicopter <i>Ingenuity</i></a></figcaption></figure>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Electric_aircraft" title="Electric aircraft">Electric aircraft</a></div>
<p>Since the beginnings of aviation, electric power for aircraft has received a great deal of experimentation. Currently, flying <a href="/wiki/Electric_aircraft" title="Electric aircraft">electric aircraft</a> include piloted and unpiloted aerial vehicles.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Spacecraft">Spacecraft</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Spacecraft"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Electrically_powered_spacecraft_propulsion" class="mw-redirect" title="Electrically powered spacecraft propulsion">Electrically powered spacecraft propulsion</a></div>
<p>Electric power has a long history of use in <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft" title="Spacecraft">spacecraft</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Ion&#95;19642&#95;65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ion_19642-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Cybulski2&#95;66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cybulski2-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The power sources used for spacecraft are batteries, solar panels and nuclear power. Current methods of propelling a spacecraft with electricity include the <a href="/wiki/Arcjet_rocket" title="Arcjet rocket">arcjet rocket</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Electrostatic_ion_thruster" class="mw-redirect" title="Electrostatic ion thruster">electrostatic ion thruster</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hall-effect_thruster" title="Hall-effect thruster">Hall-effect thruster</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Field_Emission_Electric_Propulsion" class="mw-redirect" title="Field Emission Electric Propulsion">Field Emission Electric Propulsion</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Rovers">Rovers</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Rovers"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rover_(space_exploration)" title="Rover (space exploration)">Rover (space exploration)</a></div>
<p>Electric vehicles are the only option for <a href="/wiki/Rover_(space_exploration)" title="Rover (space exploration)">rovers</a> as there is simply no <a href="/wiki/Oxygen_gas" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxygen gas">oxygen gas</a> to drive combustion engines in <a href="/wiki/Outer_space" title="Outer space">outer space</a> and <a href="/wiki/Exoplanet" title="Exoplanet">Exoplanetary</a> <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere" title="Atmosphere">atmospheres</a>. Crewed and uncrewed electric vehicles have been used to explore the <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a> and other planets in the <a href="/wiki/Solar_System" title="Solar System">Solar System</a>. On the last three missions of the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">Apollo program</a> in 1971 and 1972, <a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">astronauts</a> drove <a href="/wiki/Silver-oxide_battery" class="mw-redirect" title="Silver-oxide battery">silver-oxide battery</a>-powered <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Roving_Vehicle" title="Lunar Roving Vehicle">Lunar Roving Vehicles</a> distances up to 35.7 kilometers (22.2&#160;mi) on the lunar surface.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaics" title="Photovoltaics">Solar-powered</a>, <a href="/wiki/Teleoperation" title="Teleoperation">remotely controlled</a> uncrewed rovers have also explored the Moon and <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Charging/fueling"><span id="Charging.2Ffueling"></span>Charging/fueling</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Charging/fueling"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Stations">Stations</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Stations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>

<p>A <a href="/wiki/Charging_station" title="Charging station">charging station</a>, also known as a charge point, chargepoint, or electric vehicle supply equipment (EVSE), is a <a href="/wiki/Power_supply" title="Power supply">power supply</a> <a href="/wiki/Electrical_device" title="Electrical device">device</a> that supplies <a href="/wiki/Electrical_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Electrical power">electrical power</a> for recharging the <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_battery" title="Electric vehicle battery">onboard battery packs</a> of <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">plug-in electric vehicles</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_vehicle" title="Battery electric vehicle">battery electric vehicles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_truck" title="Electric truck">electric trucks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_bus" title="Electric bus">electric buses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neighborhood_electric_vehicle" title="Neighborhood electric vehicle">neighborhood electric vehicles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid_vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Plug-in hybrid vehicle">plug-in hybrid vehicles</a>).
</p><p>There are two main types of EV chargers: <a href="/wiki/Alternating_current" title="Alternating current">alternating current</a> (AC) charging stations and <a href="/wiki/Direct_current" title="Direct current">direct current</a> (DC) charging stations. Electric vehicle batteries can only be charged by direct current electricity, while most <a href="/wiki/Mains_electricity" title="Mains electricity">mains electricity</a> is delivered from the <a href="/wiki/Power_grid" class="mw-redirect" title="Power grid">power grid</a> as alternating current. For this reason, most electric vehicles have a built-in <a href="/wiki/AC-to-DC_converter" class="mw-redirect" title="AC-to-DC converter">AC-to-DC converter</a> commonly known as the "onboard charger" (OBC). At an AC charging station, AC power from the grid is supplied to this onboard charger, which converts it into DC power to recharge the battery. DC chargers provide higher-power charging (which requires much larger AC-to-DC converters) by integrating the converter into the charging station, thereby avoiding size, weight, and cost constraints in vehicles. The station then directly supplies DC power to the vehicle, bypassing the onboard converter. Most modern electric vehicles can accept both AC and DC power.
</p>
</div></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Battery_swapping">Battery swapping</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Battery swapping"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Instead of recharging EVs from electric sockets, batteries could be mechanically replaced at special stations in a few minutes (<a href="/wiki/Battery_swapping" title="Battery swapping">battery swapping</a>).
</p><p>Batteries with greater <a href="/wiki/Energy_density" title="Energy density">energy density</a> such as metal–air fuel cells cannot always be recharged in a purely electric way, so some form of mechanical recharge may be used instead. A <a href="/wiki/Zinc%E2%80%93air_battery" title="Zinc–air battery">zinc–air battery</a>, technically a <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell" title="Fuel cell">fuel cell</a>, is difficult to recharge electrically so may be "refueled" by periodically replacing the anode or electrolyte instead.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Bidirectional_charging">Bidirectional charging</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Bidirectional charging"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>General Motors (GM) is adding a capability called <a href="/wiki/Vehicle-to-grid" title="Vehicle-to-grid">V2H</a>, or bidirectional charging, to allow its new electric vehicles to send power from their batteries to the owner's home. GM will start with 2024 models, including the Silverado and Blazer EVs, and promises to continue the feature through to model year 2026. This could be helpful to the owner during unexpected power grid outages because an electric vehicle is a giant battery on wheels.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-bidirectional2&#95;71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bidirectional2-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Considerations">Considerations</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Considerations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
