<ul><li><span class="nowrap"><span class="noviewer" typeof="mw:File"><span title="Category"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/96/Symbol_category_class.svg/20px-Symbol_category_class.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/96/Symbol_category_class.svg/40px-Symbol_category_class.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185" /></span></span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Category:Renewable_energy" title="Category:Renewable energy">Category</a></span></li>
<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="nowrap"><span class="noviewer" typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Wind-turbine-icon.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Wind-turbine-icon.svg/20px-Wind-turbine-icon.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Wind-turbine-icon.svg/40px-Wind-turbine-icon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="128" data-file-height="128" /></a></span> </span><a href="/wiki/Portal:Renewable_energy" title="Portal:Renewable energy">Renewable energy&#32;portal</a></span></li></ul></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1333133064" /><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1239400231" /><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Sustainable_energy" title="Template:Sustainable energy"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Sustainable_energy" title="Template talk:Sustainable energy"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Template:Sustainable_energy" title="Special:EditPage/Template:Sustainable energy"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_aspects_of_the_electric_car" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental aspects of the electric car">Environmental aspects of the electric car</a>, <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impacts_of_lithium-ion_batteries" title="Environmental impacts of lithium-ion batteries">Environmental impacts of lithium-ion batteries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_the_petroleum_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental impact of the petroleum industry">Environmental impact of the petroleum industry</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Environmental_footprint_of_electric_cars" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental footprint of electric cars">Environmental footprint of electric cars</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Battery-cost-learning-curve.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Battery-cost-learning-curve.png/250px-Battery-cost-learning-curve.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="297" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Battery-cost-learning-curve.png/500px-Battery-cost-learning-curve.png 2x" data-file-width="1773" data-file-height="2106" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Learning_curve" title="Learning curve">Learning curve</a> of lithium-ion batteries: the price of batteries declined by 97% in three decades.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>EVs release no tailpipe <a href="/wiki/Air_pollutant" class="mw-redirect" title="Air pollutant">air pollutants</a>, and reduce respiratory illnesses such as <a href="/wiki/Asthma" title="Asthma">asthma</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By reducing types of air pollution, such as <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_dioxide" title="Nitrogen dioxide">nitrogen dioxide</a>, EVs could also prevent hundreds of thousands of early deaths every year,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> especially from trucks and traffic in cities.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Additionally, EVs have significantly less noise pollution in urban areas, improving the quality of life overall.
</p><p>The carbon emissions from producing and operating an EV are, in the majority of cases less, than those of producing and operating a conventional vehicle.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> When pursuing a cost-responsive electric charging strategy (instead of an emission-responsive charging strategy), considerably higher emissions might arise as embedded carbon emissions from electricity are dynamic.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> EVs in urban areas almost always pollute less than internal combustion vehicles.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>However, EVs are charged with electricity that may be <a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">generated</a> by means that have health and environmental impacts.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This is particularly relevant in places that rely on coal-powered electricity grids.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It also have negative environmental impacts due to the manufacturing and recycling of batteries. The full environmental impact of electric vehicles includes the life cycle impacts of carbon and sulfur emissions, as well as toxic metals entering the environment.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Alanazi&#95;60162&#95;84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alanazi_60162-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Despite that, ICE vehicles use far more raw materials over their lifetime than EVs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> One source estimates that over a fifth of the <a href="/wiki/Lithium" title="Lithium">lithium</a> and about 65% of the <a href="/wiki/Cobalt" title="Cobalt">cobalt</a> needed for electric cars will be from recycled sources by 2035.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-transportenvironment202103012&#95;86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transportenvironment202103012-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On the other hand, when counting the large quantities of fossil fuel non-electric cars consume over their lifetime, electric cars can be considered to dramatically reduce raw-material needs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-transportenvironment202103012&#95;86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transportenvironment202103012-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>One limitation of the environmental potential of EVs is that simply switching the existing privately owned car fleet from <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">ICEs</a> to EVs will not free up road space for <a href="/wiki/Active_mobility" title="Active mobility">active travel</a> or public transport.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Electric <a href="/wiki/Micromobility" title="Micromobility">micromobility</a> vehicles, such as e-bikes, may contribute to the decarbonisation of transport systems, especially outside of urban areas which are already well-served by public transport.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Mining,_extraction_and_production"><span id="Mining.2C_extraction_and_production"></span>Mining, extraction and production</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Mining, extraction and production"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Information regarding the sustainability of the production process of batteries has become a politically charged topic.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-AgusdinataLiuEakinRomero20182&#95;89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AgusdinataLiuEakinRomero20182-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:AGE_MATTERS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:AGE MATTERS"><span title="surely there is a lot of research by now? (April 2023)">obsolete&#160;source</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Business processes of raw material extraction in practice raise issues of transparency and accountability of the management of extractive resources. In the complex <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_supply_chain" title="Electric vehicle supply chain">supply chain</a> of lithium technology, there are diverse stakeholders representing corporate interests, public interest groups and political elites that are concerned with outcomes from the technology production and use. One possibility to achieve balanced extractive processes would be the establishment of commonly agreed-upon standards on the governance of technology worldwide.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-AgusdinataLiuEakinRomero20182&#95;89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AgusdinataLiuEakinRomero20182-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The compliance of these standards can be assessed by the Assessment of Sustainability in Supply Chains Frameworks (ASSC). Hereby, the qualitative assessment consists of examining governance and social and <a href="/wiki/Natural_environment" title="Natural environment">environmental</a> commitment. Indicators for the quantitative assessment are management systems and standards, compliance and social and environmental indicators.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The initial phase of electric vehicle production incurs an environmental cost, often referred to as a "<a href="/wiki/Carbon_debt" class="mw-redirect" title="Carbon debt">carbon debt</a>", primarily driven by the energy-intensive manufacturing of high-voltage batteries and the extraction of critical raw materials.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  Rare-earth metals (<a href="/wiki/Neodymium" title="Neodymium">neodymium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dysprosium" title="Dysprosium">dysprosium</a>) and other mined metals (copper, nickel, iron) are used by EV motors, while lithium, cobalt, manganese are used by the batteries.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2023 the US State Department said that the supply of lithium would need to increase 42-fold by 2050 globally to support a transition to clean energy.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Most of the lithium-ion battery production occurs in China, where the bulk of energy used is supplied by <a href="/wiki/Coal_power_in_China" title="Coal power in China">coal-burning power plants</a>.
</p><p>The extraction and processing of these metals contributes to habitat destruction and environmental degradation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For instance, the process of mining minerals such as <a href="/wiki/Lithium" title="Lithium">lithium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cobalt" title="Cobalt">cobalt</a>, essential components of current battery chemistries, carries significant localized environmental hazards. Lithium mining, frequently conducted using water-intensive <a href="/w/index.php?title=Brine_extraction&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Brine extraction (page does not exist)">brine extraction</a>, contributes to global carbon emissions, estimated at over 1.3&#160;million tonnes of carbon annually, with every tonne of mined lithium equating to 15 tonnes of CO<sub>2</sub> released into the atmosphere.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In regions rich in cobalt, such as the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Republic of Congo">Democratic Republic of Congo</a> (DRC), environmental costs are substantial, including <a href="/wiki/Deforestation_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Deforestation in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">deforestation</a>, habitat destruction and water pollution.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Scientists have noted high <a href="/wiki/Radioactivity" class="mw-redirect" title="Radioactivity">radioactivity</a> levels in some mining regions, and industrial processes, including the <a href="/wiki/Pulverization" class="mw-redirect" title="Pulverization">pulverization</a> of rock, release dust that causes respiratory health issues for nearby populations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Open-pit <a href="/wiki/Nickel_mining" class="mw-redirect" title="Nickel mining">nickel mining</a> has led to environmental degradation and pollution in developing countries such as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_mines_in_the_Philippines" title="List of mines in the Philippines">Philippines</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_mines_in_Indonesia" title="List of mines in Indonesia">Indonesia</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2024, nickel mining and processing was one of the main causes of <a href="/wiki/Deforestation_in_Indonesia" title="Deforestation in Indonesia">deforestation in Indonesia</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Geographical_distribution_of_the_global_battery_supply_chain.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Geographical_distribution_of_the_global_battery_supply_chain.png/250px-Geographical_distribution_of_the_global_battery_supply_chain.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="127" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Geographical_distribution_of_the_global_battery_supply_chain.png/500px-Geographical_distribution_of_the_global_battery_supply_chain.png 2x" data-file-width="1161" data-file-height="592" /></a><figcaption>Geographical distribution of the <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_supply_chain" title="Electric vehicle supply chain">global battery supply chain</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 58">&#58;&#8202;58&#8202;</span></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>In 2022, the manufacturing of an EV emitted on average around 50% more CO<sub>2</sub> than an equivalent internal combustion engine vehicle, but this difference is more than offset by the much higher emissions from the oil used in driving an internal combustion engine Vehicle over its lifetime compared to those from generating the electricity used for driving the EV.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2023, Greenpeace issued a video criticizing the view that EVs are "silver bullet for climate", arguing that the construction phase has a high environmental impact. For example, the rise in <a href="/wiki/SUV" title="SUV">SUV</a> sales by <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Motor_Company" title="Hyundai Motor Company">Hyundai</a> almost eliminate the climate benefits of passing to EV in this company, because even electric SUVs have a high carbon footprint as they consume much raw materials and energy during construction. Greenpeace proposes a <a href="/wiki/Mobility_as_a_service" title="Mobility as a service">mobility as a service</a> concept instead, based on biking, public transport and ride sharing.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Life-cycle_assessment">Life-cycle assessment</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Life-cycle assessment"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Despite the initial manufacturing footprint, a <a href="/wiki/Life-cycle_assessment" title="Life-cycle assessment">life-cycle assessment</a> (LCA) approach consistently confirms that electric vehicles yield superior overall lifetime <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> (GHG) performance compared to equivalent ICE vehicles.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The extent of the environmental benefit is intrinsically linked to the carbon intensity of the electricity grid used to power the vehicle. In regions like China, battery electric vehicles currently achieve approximately 40% lower emissions compared to ICE vehicles over their full lifespan. However, in countries with high-intensity grids, such as India, the immediate advantage is more modest, resulting in only about 20% lower emissions (saving less than 10 tonnes of CO<sub>2</sub> equivalent). This context is temporary, as significant efforts are underway globally to decarbonize electricity generation; for instance, the emissions intensity of India's grid is projected to fall by 60% by 2035, rapidly increasing the environmental benefit of electrification.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>An alternative method of sourcing essential battery materials being deliberated by the <a href="/wiki/International_Seabed_Authority" title="International Seabed Authority">International Seabed Authority</a> is <a href="/wiki/Deep_sea_mining" title="Deep sea mining">deep sea mining</a>, however carmakers are not using this as of 2023.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Regulatory mechanisms, such as the EU Battery Regulation (Regulation (EU) 2023/1542) were introduced to reduce the environmental impact.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It covers the entire battery life cycle, from design and production, "battery passports", to use and end-of-life management. There are also national policies like those in France, which cap subsidies based on vehicle production carbon intensity.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Energy_efficiency">Energy efficiency</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Energy efficiency"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>EV '<a href="/wiki/Tank-to-wheel" class="mw-redirect" title="Tank-to-wheel">tank-to-wheels</a>' efficiency is about a factor of three higher than internal combustion engine vehicles.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ec.europa.eu2&#95;38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ec.europa.eu2-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Energy is not consumed while the vehicle is stationary, unlike internal combustion engines which consume fuel while idling. In 2022, EVs enabled a net reduction of about 80 Mt of GHG emissions, on a <a href="/wiki/Well-to-wheel" class="mw-redirect" title="Well-to-wheel">well-to-wheels</a> basis, and the net GHG benefit of EVs will increase over time as the electricity sector is decarbonised.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-global-ev-outlook-20232&#95;118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-global-ev-outlook-20232-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Well-to-wheel efficiency of an EV has less to do with the vehicle itself and more to do with the method of electricity production. A particular EV would instantly become twice as efficient if electricity production were switched from fossil fuels to renewable energy, such as wind power, tidal power, solar power, and nuclear power. Thus, when "well-to-wheels" is cited, the discussion is no longer about the vehicle, but rather about the entire energy supply infrastructure&#160;&#8211;&#32;in the case of fossil fuels this should also include energy spent on exploration, mining, refining, and distribution.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The lifecycle analysis of EVs shows that even when powered by the most carbon-intensive electricity in Europe, they emit less greenhouse gases than a conventional diesel vehicle.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Range">Range</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Range"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/All-electric_range" title="All-electric range">All-electric range</a> and <a href="/wiki/Range_anxiety" title="Range anxiety">range anxiety</a></div>
<p>Electric vehicles may have shorter range compared to vehicles with internal combustion engines,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which is why the electrification of long-distance transport, such as long-distance shipping, remains challenging.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of 2025<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> practical <a href="/wiki/Electric_aircraft" title="Electric aircraft">electric aircraft</a> are small and limited to a few hundred kilometres.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Cost_of_ownership">Cost of ownership</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Cost of ownership"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Electric vehicles with low worldwide market share, such as ships,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> typically carry a higher initial purchase price than comparable ICE vehicles. This elevated upfront cost constitutes a significant barrier to entry. While long-term financial analyses may favor EVs, the immediate capital outlay often dictates purchasing decisions, slowing the pace of the overall market transition.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:02&#95;126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The higher initial price is often offset by superior total cost of ownership (TCO) over the vehicle's lifespan.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:02&#95;126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Operational expenses for EVs are markedly lower.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Battery_longevity_and_replacement">Battery longevity and replacement</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Battery longevity and replacement"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Advances in lithium-ion batteries, driven at first by the personal-use electronics industry, allow full-sized, highway-capable EVs to travel nearly as far on a single charge as conventional cars go on a single tank of gasoline. Lithium batteries have been made safe, can be recharged in minutes instead of hours (see <a href="/wiki/Rechargeable_battery#Recharging_time" title="Rechargeable battery">recharging time</a>), and now last longer than the typical vehicle (see <a href="/wiki/Rechargeable_battery#Lifespan_and_cycle_stability" title="Rechargeable battery">lifespan</a>). The production cost of these lighter, higher-capacity lithium-ion batteries is gradually decreasing as the technology matures and production volumes increase.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Research is also underway to improve battery reuse and recycling, which would further reduce the environmental impact of batteries.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Many companies and researchers are also working on newer battery technologies, including solid state batteries<sup id="cite&#95;ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and alternate technologies.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The risk of requiring an out-of-warranty battery replacement represents the greatest source of long-term financial uncertainty for many prospective EV retail owners. Despite consumer anxieties, actual battery replacement events are statistically rare, and modern EV batteries are demonstrating significantly greater durability than initially anticipated.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Studies have confirmed that EV batteries can outlast the vehicle's lifetime with minimal degradation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The financial risk associated with future replacement is collapsing due to advancements in battery manufacturing and economics.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Industry reports project that global market oversupply will persist through 2028, accelerating price reductions.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Performance_in_extreme_climates">Performance in extreme climates</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Performance in extreme climates"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Electric vehicle range and battery performance are negatively affected by extreme cold, as ambient temperatures necessitate diverting energy for cabin heating and maintaining optimal battery temperature. A comprehensive winter performance study by the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Automobile_Association" title="Canadian Automobile Association">Canadian Automobile Association</a> (CAA) revealed that cold weather significantly impacts driving range, with vehicles experiencing reductions between 14% and 39% compared to their official estimates when operated at −15<sup>∘</sup>C.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This quantifiable range loss presents a significant practical challenge for owners in cold climates. However, as the industry matures, increasing standardization and optimization of these thermal systems are expected to mitigate cold weather range anxiety.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Heating">Heating</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Heating"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Heat_pump" title="Heat pump">heat pump</a> system, capable of cooling the cabin during summer and heating it during winter, is an efficient way of heating and cooling EVs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For vehicles which are connected to the grid, battery EVs can be preheated, or cooled, with little or no need for battery energy, especially for short trips. Most new electric cars come with heat pumps as standard.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Safety">Safety</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Safety"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Electric vehicle safety regulations have evolved significantly since the initial UN ECE Regulation 100. Current regulations focus on <a href="/wiki/Thermal_runaway" title="Thermal runaway">thermal runaway</a> protection, with various international standards mandating advance warning systems and thermal propagation containment measures.
</p><p>Recent technological developments address thermal runaway concerns more proactively. Advanced fire protection materials for EV batteries have become a critical research area, with developments in ceramics, mica, aerogels, coatings, and phase change materials designed to prevent or delay thermal runaway propagation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-auto12&#95;145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto12-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Current regulations vary by region, with China being an early adopter of thermal runaway-specific requirements mandating prevention of fire or smoke exiting battery packs for five minutes after an event occurs. However, industry experts suggest longer escape times may be necessary for future regulations, with original equipment manufacturers targeting extended protection periods to pre-empt future regulatory requirements.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-auto12&#95;145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto12-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Research published in the <a href="/wiki/British_Medical_Journal" class="mw-redirect" title="British Medical Journal">British Medical Journal</a> indicates that electric cars hit pedestrians at twice the rate of petrol or diesel vehicles due to being quieter.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Repair_shops">Repair shops</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Repair shops"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The infrastructure for vehicle repairs after accidents is a concern for insurers and mechanics due to safety requirements.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>147<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Although no fatalities have been reported in electric vehicle repair till year 2024, repairing the high voltage battery includes <a href="/wiki/Electrical_injury" title="Electrical injury">electrical injury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arc_flash" title="Arc flash">arc flash</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thermal_runaway" title="Thermal runaway">fire hazard</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>148<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Batteries and other components must be carefully evaluated rather than being totally written off by <a href="/wiki/Claims_adjuster" class="mw-redirect" title="Claims adjuster">insurers</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>149<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Socio-economic">Socio-economic</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Socio-economic"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>A 2003 study in the United Kingdom found that "[p]ollution is most concentrated in areas where young children and their parents are more likely to live and least concentrated in areas to which the elderly tend to migrate," and that "those communities that are most polluted and which also emit the least pollution tend to be amongst the poorest in Britain."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>150<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A 2019 UK study found that "households in the poorest areas emit the least NOx and PM, whilst the least poor areas emitted the highest, per km, vehicle emissions per household through having higher vehicle ownership, owning more diesel vehicles and driving further."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>151<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The transport planner, <a href="/wiki/Karel_Martens_(transport_planner)" title="Karel Martens (transport planner)">Karel Martens</a>, in a 2009 article warned that electric vehicles only solve the problem of emissions by cars while not solving or improving their impact on the amount of space used by cars or <a href="/wiki/Parking" title="Parking">parking</a> issues. Martens who is of the field of <a href="/wiki/Transport_Justice:_Designing_fair_transportation_systems" title="Transport Justice: Designing fair transportation systems">Transport Justice</a>, also said that electric vehicles do not improve accessibility to people who do not own cars.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:32&#95;152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:32-152"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>152<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:42&#95;153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:42-153"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>153<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Government_incentivization">Government incentivization</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Government incentivization"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_incentives_for_plug-in_electric_vehicles" title="Government incentives for plug-in electric vehicles">Government incentives for plug-in electric vehicles</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Electric_car_use_by_country" title="Electric car use by country">Electric car use by country</a></div>
<p>The IEA suggests that taxing inefficient internal combustion engine vehicles could encourage adoption of EVs, with taxes raised being used to fund subsidies for EVs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-global-ev-outlook-20232&#95;118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-global-ev-outlook-20232-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Government procurement is sometimes used to encourage national EV manufacturers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>154<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Many countries will <a href="/wiki/Phase-out_of_fossil_fuel_vehicles" title="Phase-out of fossil fuel vehicles">ban sales of fossil fuel road vehicles</a> between 2025 and 2040.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Many governments offer incentives to promote the use of electric vehicles, with the goals of reducing air pollution and oil consumption. Some incentives intend to increase purchases of electric vehicles by offsetting the purchase price with a grant. Other incentives include lower tax rates or exemption from certain taxes, and investment in charging infrastructure.
</p><p>As of 2025<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> most European countries offer financial incentives to encourage commercial EV adoption.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>157<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Partnerships between EV manufacturers and utility companies have also provided incentives and sales on EV purchases to promote cleaner energy usage and transportation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-US&#95;EPA2&#95;158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_EPA2-158"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>158<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Companies selling EVs have partnered with local <a href="/wiki/Electric_utilities" class="mw-redirect" title="Electric utilities">electric utilities</a> to provide large incentives on some electric vehicles.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>159<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Infrastructure_management">Infrastructure management</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Infrastructure management"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>With the increase in number of electric vehicles, it is necessary to create an appropriate number of <a href="/wiki/Charging_station" title="Charging station">charging stations</a> to supply the increasing demand.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>160<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>161<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> While the deployment of public charging infrastructure is accelerating globally, the adoption rate of EVs risks outpacing network expansion, leading to potential future congestion. Experts concur that large-scale EV adoption will inevitably stress local distribution networks if charging is conducted randomly during peak hours of electricity demand. This unmanaged demand risks <a href="/wiki/Grid_energy_storage" title="Grid energy storage">grid</a> instability and necessitates proactive management from utilities.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>162<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the United States, charging ports saw quarterly increases between 4.6% and 6.3% in early 2024. However, projections indicate a measurable risk of insufficient density. In the US, the ratio of electric light-duty vehicles per public charging point is projected to climb dramatically from approximately 18:1 in 2023 to over 80:1 by 2035 . This sharply increasing ratio confirms that current deployment, while active, may be structurally insufficient to prevent charging queues unless aggressive government targets, such as the US objective of 500,000 public charging ports by 2030, are met and exceeded.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>163<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Countering_systemic_bias" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Countering systemic bias"><span title="The material near this tag may not represent a worldwide view of the subject. (March 2026)">globalize</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Policy mandates are driving targeted deployment to alleviate infrastructure pressure. Countries like India have set requirements for installing chargers every 25 km along major highways.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:12&#95;164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-164"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>164<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Logistical hurdles regarding charge times are being addressed by rapid advancements in charging technology. Commercially available DC fast charging stations currently deliver 250–350 kW, and regulatory frameworks, such as the EU's Alternative Fuels Infrastructure Regulation (AFIR), are preparing for the eventual commercialization of 1 MW charging stations. The transition to 1 MW charging, however, requires significant investment in both installation and grid upgrades.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:12&#95;164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-164"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>164<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Stabilization_of_the_grid">Stabilization of the grid</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Stabilization of the grid"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:V2GEnabledEVFastCharger.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/V2GEnabledEVFastCharger.jpg/250px-V2GEnabledEVFastCharger.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="377" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/V2GEnabledEVFastCharger.jpg/500px-V2GEnabledEVFastCharger.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="4928" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Vehicle-to-grid" title="Vehicle-to-grid">Vehicle-to-grid</a> (V2G) charger where energy can flow back into the grid if needed</figcaption></figure>
<p>Since EVs can be plugged into the <a href="/wiki/Electric_grid" class="mw-redirect" title="Electric grid">electric grid</a> when not in use, battery-powered vehicles could reduce the need for <a href="/wiki/Dispatchable_generation" title="Dispatchable generation">dispatchable generation</a> by feeding electricity into the grid from their batteries during periods of high demand and low supply (such as just after sunset) while doing most of their charging at night or midday, when there is unused generating capacity.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Liasi2&#95;165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Liasi2-165"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>165<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>166<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This <a href="/wiki/Vehicle-to-grid" title="Vehicle-to-grid">vehicle-to-grid</a> (V2G) connection has the potential to reduce the need for new power plants, as long as vehicle owners do not mind reducing the life of their batteries, by being drained by the power company during peak demand. Electric vehicle parking lots can provide <a href="/wiki/Demand_response" title="Demand response">demand response</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Shafie-khah&#95;Heydarian-Forushani&#95;20162&#95;167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shafie-khah_Heydarian-Forushani_20162-167"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>167<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Current electricity infrastructure may need to cope with increasing shares of variable-output power sources such as wind and <a href="/wiki/Solar_PV" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar PV">solar</a>. This variability could be addressed by adjusting the speed at which EV batteries are charged, or possibly even discharged.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>168<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Some concepts see battery exchanges and battery charging stations, much like gas/petrol stations today. These will require enormous storage and charging potentials, which could be manipulated to vary the rate of charging, and to output power during shortage periods, much as diesel generators are used for short periods to stabilize some national grids.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>169<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>170<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="In-development_technologies">In-development technologies</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: In-development technologies"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Electric_double-layer_capacitor" class="mw-redirect" title="Electric double-layer capacitor">Electric double-layer capacitor</a></div>
<p>Conventional electric double-layer capacitors (<a href="/wiki/Supercapacitor" title="Supercapacitor">supercapacitors</a>) continue to be developed to achieve higher energy densities while maintaining their characteristic fast charging capabilities and extended lifespans. Recent research has focused on solid-state supercapacitor configurations that eliminate liquid electrolytes, providing enhanced safety and design flexibility.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>171<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Advanced developments include all-graphene oxide flexible solid-state supercapacitors with enhanced electrochemical performance, achieving areal capacitances of 14.5 mF cm⁻² among the highest values for any graphene-based supercapacitor.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>172<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Recent breakthroughs include dual storage mechanism nanoscale solid-state lithium-ion supercapacitors using atomic layer deposition-synthesized lithium phosphorus oxynitride (LiPON) as solid-state electrolyte, demonstrating capacitance densities of 500 nF·mm⁻² with excellent cycling stability over ten thousand cycles.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>173<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> High-performance solid-state supercapacitors have been developed using silicon electrodes with graphene interconnected networks, showing remarkable performance characteristics comparable to high-power carbon-based supercapacitors.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>174<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Advanced hybrid designs include all-solid-state planar micro-supercapacitors based on 2D vanadium nitride nanosheets and cobalt hydroxide nanoflowers, achieving energy densities of 12.4 mWh cm⁻³ and power densities of 1,750&#160;mW cm⁻³.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>175<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Flexible solid-state supercapacitors operating across wide temperature ranges from -70&#160;°C to 220&#160;°C have been demonstrated using polycation-polybenzimidazole blend electrolytes doped with phosphoric acid.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>176<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Battery_advancements">Battery advancements</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Battery advancements"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><b>Solid-state batteries</b> represent one of the most promising next-generation battery technologies, offering potential advantages over conventional lithium-ion batteries including higher energy density, faster charging, improved safety, and longer lifespan. According to a comprehensive review in Chemical Engineering Journal, all-solid-state lithium batteries using solid electrolytes are regarded as the next generation of energy storage devices, with recent breakthroughs significantly accelerating their path toward commercial viability.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>177<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Fraunhofer ISI Solid-State Battery Roadmap 2035+,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>178<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> developed with contributions from more than 100 European experts, provides a comprehensive assessment of solid-state battery development potential over the next decade, benchmarking against established lithium-ion batteries.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>179<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to market analysis published in Scientific Talks, solid-state batteries are projected to reach mass production with costs of 140–175 USD per kWh by 2028–2030, depending on technological and manufacturing challenges.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>180<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Recent commercial developments include Mercedes-Benz and Factorial Energy conducting road tests of <a href="/wiki/Semi-solid-state_batteries" class="mw-redirect" title="Semi-solid-state batteries">semi-solid-state batteries</a> in the EQS sedan, promising a 25% increase in range with energy densities of 391 watt-hours per kilogram. This represents the world's first integration of lithium-metal solid-state batteries into a production vehicle.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>181<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, according to IEEE Spectrum analysis, solid-state batteries face significant "production hell" challenges, with experts noting pointed skepticism toward current technical announcements and the engineering obstacles that lie ahead.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>182<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Toyota continues to lead development efforts, targeting solid-state battery production by 2027–2028 with goals of 1,000&#160;km range and 10-minute fast charging capabilities. The company claims recent technological advancements have overcome previous battery life trade-offs and switched focus to mass production readiness.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>183<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Research published in ACS Energy Letters emphasizes that while all-solid-state batteries show promise for electric vehicles, significant challenges remain in Li-metal implementation, interfacial stability, and large-scale manufacturing.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>184<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sodium-ion_battery" title="Sodium-ion battery">Sodium-ion batteries</a> continue to show promise with potential energy densities of 400&#160;Wh/kg and minimal expansion/contraction during charge cycles, while relying on more abundant and cost-effective materials than lithium-ion technology. Recent research published in Energy &amp; Fuels highlights sodium-ion and all-solid-state sodium batteries as promising choices for future energy storage systems due to abundant sodium resources and lower costs compared to lithium-based systems.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>185<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Battery_management_and_intermediate_storage">Battery management and intermediate storage</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Battery management and intermediate storage"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Another improvement is to decouple the electric motor from the battery through electronic control, using <a href="/wiki/Supercapacitor" title="Supercapacitor">supercapacitors</a> to buffer large but short power demands and <a href="/wiki/Regenerative_braking" title="Regenerative braking">regenerative braking</a> energy.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>186<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The development of new cell types combined with intelligent cell management improved both weak points mentioned above. The cell management involves not only monitoring the health of the cells but also a redundant cell configuration (one more cell than needed). With sophisticated switched wiring, it is possible to condition one cell while the rest are on duty.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Electric_roads">Electric roads</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Electric roads"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Electric_road" title="Electric road">Electric road</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Electric_road_systems.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Electric_road_systems.svg/250px-Electric_road_systems.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="375" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Electric_road_systems.svg/500px-Electric_road_systems.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="1920" /></a><figcaption>Three types of electric road systems. An electric bus (black) receives power from the road: (A) with three <a href="/wiki/Inductive_charging#Transportation" title="Inductive charging">inductive pickups</a> (red) from a strip of resonant inductive coils (blue) embedded several centimeters under the road (gray); (B) with a <a href="/wiki/Current_collector" title="Current collector">current collector</a> (red) sliding over a <a href="/wiki/Ground-level_power_supply" title="Ground-level power supply">ground-level power supply</a> rail segment (blue) flush with the surface of the road (gray); (C) with an overhead current collector (red) sliding against a powered <a href="/wiki/Overhead_line" title="Overhead line">overhead line</a> (blue)</figcaption></figure>
<p>An electric road system (ERS) is a road which supplies electric power to vehicles travelling on it. Common implementations are <a href="/wiki/Overhead_line" title="Overhead line">overhead power lines</a> above the road, <a href="/wiki/Ground-level_power_supply" title="Ground-level power supply">ground-level power supply</a> through conductive rails, and dynamic wireless power transfer (DWPT) through <a href="/wiki/Inductive_charging#Transportation" title="Inductive charging">resonant inductive coils</a> or inductive rails embedded in the road. Overhead power lines are limited to commercial vehicles while ground-level rails and inductive power transfer can be used by any vehicle, which allows for public charging through a power metering and billing systems. Of the three methods, ground-level conductive rails are estimated to be the most cost-effective.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Fernandez2&#95;187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fernandez2-187"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>187<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 10–11">&#58;&#8202;10–11&#8202;</span></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="National_electric_road_projects">National electric road projects</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: National electric road projects"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Government studies and trials have been conducted in several countries seeking a national electric road system (ERS) network.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">Korea</a> was the first to implement an induction-based public electric road with a commercial bus line in 2013 after testing an experimental shuttle service in 2009,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-TRL2&#95;188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TRL2-188"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>188<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 11–18">&#58;&#8202;11–18&#8202;</span></sup> but it was shut down due to aging infrastructure amidst controversy over the continued public funding of the technology.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-korea-controversy2&#95;189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-korea-controversy2-189"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>189<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>United Kingdom municipal projects in 2015<sup id="cite&#95;ref-uk-budget2&#95;190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uk-budget2-190"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>190<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and 2021 found wireless electric roads financially unfeasible.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-uk-expensive2&#95;191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uk-expensive2-191"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>191<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Transport_Administration_electric_road_program" title="Swedish Transport Administration electric road program">Swedish Transport Administration electric road program</a> started assessing electric road systems (ERS) in 2013.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-businessmodel2&#95;192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-businessmodel2-192"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>192<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 5">&#58;&#8202;5&#8202;</span></sup> After receiving ERS construction offers in excess of the project's budget in 2023, Sweden pursued cost-reduction measures for either <a href="/wiki/Inductive_charging#Transportation" title="Inductive charging">wireless ERS</a> or <a href="/wiki/Ground-level_power_supply" title="Ground-level power supply">rail ERS</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-cost20232&#95;193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cost20232-193"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>193<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The project's final report, published in 2024, recommended against funding a national ERS in Sweden as it would not be cost-effective, unless the technology was adopted by its trading partners such as by France and Germany. Following the report, the project was paused.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-2024-summary2&#95;194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2024-summary2-194"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>194<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-2024-full-report2&#95;195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2024-full-report2-195"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>195<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>196<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Germany found in 2023 that the wireless electric road system (wERS) by Electreon collects 64.3% of the transmitted energy, poses many difficulties during installation, and blocks access to other infrastructure in the road.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-WPTCE-japan-20242&#95;197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WPTCE-japan-20242-197"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>197<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Germany trialed overhead lines in three projects in the 2010s and 2020s and reported they are too expensive, difficult to maintain, and pose a safety risk.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-germany-end2&#95;198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-germany-end2-198"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>198<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-germany-overhead-difficulties2&#95;199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-germany-overhead-difficulties2-199"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>199<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-germany-overhead-safety2&#95;200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-germany-overhead-safety2-200"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>200<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>France found similar drawbacks for overhead lines as Germany did. <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_France#Electric_roads" title="Transport in France">France began several electric road pilot projects in 2023</a> for inductive and rail systems.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-usinenouvelle-may-20242&#95;201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usinenouvelle-may-20242-201"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>201<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ground-level_power_supply" title="Ground-level power supply">Ground-level power supply</a> systems are considered the most likely candidates.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ers-france-20222&#95;202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ers-france-20222-202"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>202<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="See_also">See also</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: See also"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>

data-file-height="219" /></span></span></span><span class="portalbox-link"><a href="/wiki/Portal:Cars" title="Portal:Cars">Cars portal</a></span></li><li class="portalbox-entry"><span <li id="cite&#95;note-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-50">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1333433106" /><cite id="CITEREFDomonoske2021" class="citation news cs1">Domonoske, Camila (17 March 2021). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.npr.org/2021/03/17/976152350/from-amazon-to-fedex-the-delivery-truck-is-going-electric">"From Amazon To FedEx, The Delivery Truck Is Going Electric"</a>. National Public Radio<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">13 June</span> 2021</span>. <q>All major delivery companies are starting to replace their gas-powered fleets with electric or low-emission vehicles, a switch that companies say will boost their bottom lines, while also fighting climate change and urban pollution. UPS has placed an order for 10,000 electric delivery vehicles. Amazon is buying 100,000 from the start-up Rivian. DHL says zero-emission vehicles make up a fifth of its fleet, with more to come. And FedEx just pledged to replace 100% of its pickup and delivery fleet with battery-powered vehicles.</q></cite><span title="ctx&#95;ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft&#95;val&#95;fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.atitle=From+Amazon+To+FedEx%2C+The+Delivery+Truck+Is+Going+Electric&amp;rft.date=2021-03-17&amp;rft.aulast=Domonoske&amp;rft.aufirst=Camila&amp;rft&#95;id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.npr.org%2F2021%2F03%2F17%2F976152350%2Ffrom-amazon-to-fedex-the-delivery-truck-is-going-electric&amp;rfr&#95;id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AElectric+vehicle" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-51">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1333433106" /><cite id="CITEREFJoselow2020" class="citation news cs1">Joselow, Maxine (11 January 2020). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.scientificamerican.com/article/delivery-vehicles-increasingly-choke-cities-with-pollution/">"Delivery Vehicles Increasingly Choke Cities with Pollution"</a>. Scientific American<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">13 June</span> 2021</span>. <q>Electric vehicles, delivery drones and rules on when delivery trucks can operate are some solutions proposed in a new report. The report provides 24 recommendations for policymakers and the private sector, including mandating that delivery vehicles are electric. The report notes that if policymakers care about sustainability, they may want to impose aggressive new electric vehicle regulations.</q></cite><span title="ctx&#95;ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft&#95;val&#95;fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.atitle=Delivery+Vehicles+Increasingly+Choke+Cities+with+Pollution&amp;rft.date=2020-01-11&amp;rft.aulast=Joselow&amp;rft.aufirst=Maxine&amp;rft&#95;id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.scientificamerican.com%2Farticle%2Fdelivery-vehicles-increasingly-choke-cities-with-pollution%2F&amp;rfr&#95;id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AElectric+vehicle" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-52">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1333433106" /><cite id="CITEREFGies2017" class="citation news cs1">Gies, Erica (18 December 2017). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://insideclimatenews.org/news/18122017/electric-truck-urban-package-delivery-ups-tesla-semi-daimler-byd-china-battery/">"Electric Trucks Begin Reporting for Duty, Quietly and Without All the Fumes"</a>. Inside Climate News<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">13 June</span> 2021</span>. <q>Replacing fleets of medium- and heavy-duty trucks can help cut greenhouse gas emissions and make cities quieter and cleaner. Because trucks need so much hauling power, they have eluded electrification until recently; a battery that could pull significant weight would itself be too hefty and too expensive. But now, improvements in battery technology are paying off, bringing down both size and cost. The number of hybrid-electric and electric trucks is set to grow almost 25 percent annually, from 1 percent of the market in 2017 to 7 percent in 2027, a jump from about 40,000 electric trucks worldwide this year to 371,000.</q></cite><span title="ctx&#95;ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft&#95;val&#95;fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.atitle=Electric+Trucks+Begin+Reporting+for+Duty%2C+Quietly+and+Without+All+the+Fumes&amp;rft.date=2017-12-18&amp;rft.aulast=Gies&amp;rft.aufirst=Erica&amp;rft&#95;id=https%3A%2F%2Finsideclimatenews.org%2Fnews%2F18122017%2Felectric-truck-urban-package-delivery-ups-tesla-semi-daimler-byd-china-battery%2F&amp;rfr&#95;id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AElectric+vehicle" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-53"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-53">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1333433106" /><cite class="citation news cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20110727110924/http://namti.org/?page_id=9">"-Maglev Technology Explained"</a>. <i>North American Maglev Transport Institute</i>. 1 January 2011.
